  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7df2a321-d942-4fa2-8b07-d17699f3b3c7'
      });

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/597740-must-you-read-the-first-two-books-to">Must you read the first two books to understand this one? Can you read them out of order??</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_597740'><a id="like_count_community_question_597740" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/597740?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F10165761-quintana-of-charyn">like</a></span>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5861997-kiersten"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1323835889i/5861997._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5861997-kiersten">Kiersten</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You definitely must read at least the second book (<i>Froi of the Exiles</i>) first. It has unresolved plot threads and several cliffhangers that will make t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You definitely must read at least the second book (<i>Froi of the Exiles</i>) first. It has unresolved plot threads and several cliffhangers that will make the third book really confusing if you haven't read it. You could probably follow <i>Froi</i> and <i>Quintana</i> together without reading the first book (<i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>), which is more of a standalone novel, but I would recommend reading all three in order for the best understanding. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_242525078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242525078" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242525078?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=australian-writer">australian-writer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242525078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9165143614578150353">Quintana of Charyn is a masterful novel. Hauntingly beautiful, powerfully written and the perfect end to this brilliant fantasy series.<br/><br/>But this is nothing different. Marchetta's novels only come in shades of amazing. By far her strongest and most compelling ability as a writer, is the way in which she crafts her characters and their struggles in the context of the world they live in.<br/><br/>If you have read Finnikin of the Rock and Froi of the Exiles than fear not. Quintana of Charyn will not disappoint</span>
  <span id="freeText9165143614578150353" style="display:none">Quintana of Charyn is a masterful novel. Hauntingly beautiful, powerfully written and the perfect end to this brilliant fantasy series.<br /><br />But this is nothing different. Marchetta's novels only come in shades of amazing. By far her strongest and most compelling ability as a writer, is the way in which she crafts her characters and their struggles in the context of the world they live in.<br /><br />If you have read Finnikin of the Rock and Froi of the Exiles than fear not. Quintana of Charyn will not disappoint.<br /><br />What sets the Lumatere series apart from many other fantasy novels is it's focus on people and relationships. It's easy, when constructing fantasy worlds, foreign mythology and ensuring you've described the elves' ears right, to forget the heart and soul of fantasy - and that is the people in it. Who are they? what are their struggles? What do they hope for? What do they fear? Often societies and races get boiled down to the language lexicon and dress code that the author painstakingly put aside for them.<br /><br />There is a rich, imaginative fantasy mythos going on here, but world-building is like movie special-effects. It's usually doing it's job best when you can't tell it's there. When it's so native and natural to the storytelling, that the audience is able to completely forget that it's all made up.<br /><br />But you guys don't really want to read my wax poetic about how much I love and respect Marchetta. Wait, you do? Okay. Here goes.<br /><br />Reading this book was like looking at a rainbow - beautiful, something for everyone, filling our hearts with joy, and you assume at least one Unicorn was involved in the making of it.<br /><br />Reading this book is like being under a spell. It doesn't seem possible, there's magic in the air, and Marchetta eats your heart with how lovely and sad it is.<br /><br />Reading this book is like having all the fun of sex without pregnancy or STDs. It'll make you cry out, beg and pray to a deity - whether you believe in one or not.<br /><br />The complaint I hear most often is that Marchetta's books are expensive - especially for non Australians. But look at it this way: Marchetta is like Hipster gold. Brilliant, obscure and hard to get. Do yourself a favour. If you've not read her books before, get them. See for yourself what all the raving is about. Fall in love again, and again. Grow up and learn, live, cry, make a bunch of life-long friends, and then do it all again with the next book.<br /><br />I promise you, Marchetta's books are worth it.<br /><br />This review can also be found on my blog, <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/10/book-review-quintana-by-melina-marchetta/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a><br /> <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9165143614578150353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_251830974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251830974" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251830974?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251830974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4402593408147451448">I am a little unsure about this rating because it's Melina Marchetta - how can her books be anything less than five stars? She's the queen of young adult who can jump across genres and still create something spectacular. But, though I really enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_' title='Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Quintana of Charyn</a>, I liked it significantly less than the other books in this series (particularly <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a>) and I think I can quite easily pinpoint the main problem: the plot. Or lack thereof. Where I think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a> could easily</span>
  <span id="freeText4402593408147451448" style="display:none">I am a little unsure about this rating because it's Melina Marchetta - how can her books be anything less than five stars? She's the queen of young adult who can jump across genres and still create something spectacular. But, though I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_" title="Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of Charyn</a>, I liked it significantly less than the other books in this series (particularly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>) and I think I can quite easily pinpoint the main problem: the plot. Or lack thereof. Where I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> could easily be read and enjoyed without reading the first book, this installment was far from the same. In fact, this book is an entirely different creature; brilliant, in its own way, but still not as strong, in my opinion.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> was a brilliantly complex novel that took us into the heart of Charyn and introduced us to life and politics within its borders. It was such a fantastic novel that I remembered exactly what happened in it without needing a recap, and it also made me completely fall in love with Froi. And he is still my favourite character after finishing this novel because of his many sides, his issues and his complicated background. The road for him has been difficult and he's done many bad things on his way to where he is now... and yet he has earned redemption - in my eyes, anyway. But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_" title="Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of Charyn</a> is a far less plot-focused story, no more main characters are introduced and the story progresses only slightly from where it's prequel finished.<br /><br />In this book, Marchetta focuses on what she already has and builds on it. Relationships are developed and explored, loyalty is questioned, opinions of certain people start to change. Almost everyone is challenged mentally and physically in this book and the characters experience a very emotional journey. It is, for me, Marchetta's most romantic novel to date. And the one with the most sex scenes. When it comes to Marchetta, neither of these is a complaint because she handles them masterfully, depicting love and sexual relationships in a very honest way that I really appreciate. The saucy scenes include bathtubs and a "game" between Finnikin and Isaboe - you know you're curious.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_" title="Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of Charyn</a> wraps things up well but I think the land of Lumatere (and all the Skuldenore lands) still has a lot more stories to tell and I hope Marchetta will return to this beautiful story. One of my biggest complaints about this book is that the title character doesn't appear in it anywhere near as much as I'd like. Quintana really interests me and the glimpses of her character just made me more curious; I think if this book was told mostly from her point of view, then she could have been a character I loved even more. But I understand that Marchetta had many different stories to address about many different people in this novel.<br /><br />Marchetta has definitely not let me down, even though I couldn't love it as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>. This woman is truly amazing and I cannot wait to see what she produces in the future. Bye bye, Lumatere *sob*</span>
  <a data-text-id="4402593408147451448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=autobuy-authors">autobuy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=romance-i-root-for">romance-i-root-for</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1012960223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11502303554757751337"><b>Reread 09/26</b> : As if I could stop at the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a>. <i>Please.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Our bodies aren't strangers," he said, his voice ragged. "Our spirits aren't strangers". He held her face in his hands. "Tell me what part of me is stranger to you and I'll destroy that part of me."</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Original review</b> : <i>Truth to be told, I was wary at first, out of fear to be disappointed by this last journey through Lumatere and Charyn. <b>I couldn't have been more wrong - indeed</b></i><b> Quintana of Charyn <i> was wonderful, as it co</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText11502303554757751337" style="display:none"><b>Reread 09/26</b> : As if I could stop at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>. <i>Please.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Our bodies aren't strangers," he said, his voice ragged. "Our spirits aren't strangers". He held her face in his hands. "Tell me what part of me is stranger to you and I'll destroy that part of me."</b>
</blockquote><br><b>Original review</b> : <i>Truth to be told, I was wary at first, out of fear to be disappointed by this last journey through Lumatere and Charyn. <b>I couldn't have been more wrong - indeed</b></i><b> Quintana of Charyn <i> was wonderful, as it contains all that I wanted and even more</i></b><i> : painful at times, heartbreaking, hilarious, I felt all kind of emotions and wasn't always able to control them. This book was beautiful.</i><br> <br><b>Let's deliver some awards, okay?</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422726063i/13538676._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Because people aren't interested in the truth, Dafar. They're interested in what keeps them safe. They're interested in being looked after. They're interested in a tale being spun."</b>
</blockquote><br>✭ <b>
  <u>Top 4 of the best meetings</u>
</b> - you know the feeling - you've started to care for several characters in the first two books and then you get to watch their meeting. <i>Precious</i>.<br>- <b>Perri and Quintana</b>. Adorable and filled with daggers (yes, that's possible) <br>- <b>Finn and Gargarin</b>. <i>Men.</i> Nothing more important to do than arguing about mythology. Did I mention that I loved them? <br>- <b>Quintana and Lucian</b>. Hilariously inappropriate - this meeting took the form of a not-so-constructive discussion about Lucian's sex performances. <i>Yeah, you heard me.</i><br>- <b>The Turlan lads and the stupid Lasconian</b>. Is it wrong I smiled so big when they defeated these annoying pricks? Take that for Froi! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Finnikin laughed. "All I had to do was stop the horse and say, 'I think...' and they were racing back into the woods to you."</b>
</blockquote><br>✭ <b>Into the category of "words I wouldn't want to use but couldn't help but laugh about"</b>, the winner is <b>Quintana</b> with her constant use of <i>"swiving"</i>.<br><br>✭ <b>Into the category of "you made me want to throw my book on the wall"</b>, the winner is <b>Queen Isaboe</b> whose decisions if understandable stayed often incredibly annoying.<br><br>✭ <b>Into the category of the best bromance scene</b>, the winners are <b>Froi and Finnikin</b> for the "you fainted/No, I didn't" scene.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You're not going to start crying, are you, fool? Quintana asked bluntly. "It irritates me".<br>Tessadora made a clucking sound of annoyance.<br>"What did I tell you?" she said to Quintana in a reprimanding voice." </b>
</blockquote><br>✭ Now, <b>into the category of the incredible characters</b>, because they've all their story to tell and because each and every one of them earned a little piece of my heart, the winners are : <br><br>- <b>Lucian</b> for the most bittersweet monologues and the way he can't help but care.<br>- <b>Phaedra</b> because <i>maaan</i>, did this girl had patience to stand these Charyn whinnies.<br>- <b>Finnikin</b> because he's a ray of light in the story - adorable and kind, comprehensive and patient, this <i>ginger cat</i> ← <i>love the surname, by the way</i>. <br>- <b>Perri</b> because every story needs his blunt guy.<br>- <b>Lirah</b> because she refuses stereotypes and for her half-mean, half-hilarious protective comments.<br>- <b>Froi</b>, of course, for his courage, his loyalty, his selflessness and his perseverance - because his quest to be accepted for who he truly is moved me like nobody else could. <br><br>✭ Yet surprisingly, despite the fact that Froi stole my heart, <b>into the category of the <i>loved-whatever-it-takes</i> character</b>, the winner is <b>Quintana</b> because she's deliciously inappropriate, refreshingly selfish, fierce, proud, courageous, in a nutshell : <b>insanely amazing</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Because he sang for Quintana of Charyn. He sang for the misery of her life, the poison in her body, the scars on her skin, and the courage in her character."</b>
</blockquote><br>✭ And finally, <b>into the category of best adorable support</b>, the winner are my boyfriend because he stand my "OMG! FROI!" and other irrepressible giggles I let out during hours, and my lovely Chelsea because I spammed her with the same thoughts. Sorry about that. <br><br><u>PS</u> : I saved so many quotes that it was really hard for me to refrain myself here. I <i>did</i> refrain, even if it seems I'm spamming you ;)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"He couldn't think, and he couldn't breathe ; his head, his chest, everthing felt as if it would explode, and he tried to count, tried to remember anythink..."</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434546074i/15235264._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437141825i/15542036._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_222099950" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222099950" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222099950?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222099950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11713419522358838136"><b>This poem does not contain spoilers for Quintana HOWEVER if you haven't read <em>Froi of the Exiles</em>, be off with you. Shoo.</b><br/><br/><em>Here she is. Crazy as ever…</em><br/><br/>You may think that it would be difficult to get behind<br/>A heroine who <em>snarls</em> at people, keeping them at arm’s length.<br/>But, for me at least, Quintana will always be my ultimate heroine,<br/>As she’s a girl who survives because of her resilience and strength.<br/><br/><em>And</em> I want her to be my life coach, my best friend,<br/>Because I can’t imagine a life without her savage litt</span>
  <span id="freeText11713419522358838136" style="display:none"><b>This poem does not contain spoilers for Quintana HOWEVER if you haven't read <em>Froi of the Exiles</em>, be off with you. Shoo.</b><br><br><em>Here she is. Crazy as ever…</em><br><br>You may think that it would be difficult to get behind<br>A heroine who <em>snarls</em> at people, keeping them at arm’s length.<br>But, for me at least, Quintana will always be my ultimate heroine,<br>As she’s a girl who survives because of her resilience and strength.<br><br><em>And</em> I want her to be my life coach, my best friend,<br>Because I can’t imagine a life without her savage little stare.<br>(I also feel it’s of the utmost importance that a girl from<br>Manchester knows how to kill, gut and skin a hare.)<br><br>I adored how we, with the help of first person account,<br>Are allowed to creep inside the madness of our girl Q.<br>We get to see what makes her heart beat (or maybe...who makes it beat.)<br>And it’s easy to see there is a little Quintana in both me and in you.<br><br>But I guess this leads me to the only quibble that I have with this book.<br><em>Gasp.</em> I know! Sacrilege. But…. OK, it’s the name.<br>Because this book may be about our crazy queen.<br>But there were other stories and I loved them all the same.<br><br>This is the story of Phaedra and the girls in the valley.<br>And it’s about the Charynites who fought for peace.<br>It’s about a woman full of anger and a bitter man, and the one they both adore.<br>And Luci-en; possibly the <em>only</em> guy who could look hot in a fleece.<br><br>And it’s about the <em>“ginger king”</em> and his beloved queen,<br>Who made me hate them one minute but love them the next.<br>The couple who started it all and hold everyone together.<br>With a love so fierce and pure and mind-blowingly complex.<br><br>And let’s not forget about the powerful white witch<br>Who keeps a warrior as her lover, the one with the scar.<br>And “<em>our boy</em>”, my favourite, with the story like no other,<br>He grew up to be pretty much everything, not at all “Dafar”.<br><br>This book isn’t about just one girl and what she does,<br>It’s about hundreds of voices, greater than the sum of their parts.<br>And it’s <em>that</em> that makes MM the queen of writing about families,<br>Friends, lovers and enemies and the connections of their hearts.<br><br><em>Q of C</em> is about journeys, both of the physical and mental.<br>It’s about not giving up for the one you love, no matter how much you’ve bled.<br>It’s about connections, circumstances and trusting those you never did.<br>OH and it also has girls telling the boys <em>exactly</em> how they want to be treated in the marital bed.<br><br>I was genuinely concerned that crafty Double M<br>Would end this series in a way that would make it difficult for me to cope.<br>And while I do <em>not</em> want to spoil this book for you…<br>I can divulge that there’s an ending full of <em>“Hope. Hope. Hope.”</em><br><br>Words or pitiful rhyme cannot express how much I adore this<br>Series and the characters that live within these pages.<br>And I have a horrible feeling that if I want to read something<br>That will affect me like this series has, I will be waiting ages.<br><br>Why do I always feel like this after I finish fantasy books?<br>The ones that speak to me the most, that make me cry and smile.<br>It’s because, I think, that they’re the books that let me<br>Escape from reality… if only for a little while.<br><br>I am distraught that it’s over but I know I will revisit Skuldenore<br>And catch up with <s>Froi</s>, <s>Lucian</s>, <s>Gargarin… is that odd?</s>, <s>Trevanion completely and utterly</s>, <s>how old is Jory? Forget I said anything… unless he’s about 20. Then we are a-go!</s>  all my old friends and greet them with my arms open wide,<br>Because all I have to do is visit my bookshelf, and once again I’ll be back with them.<br>And that’s <em>me</em> looking on that wonderful, wonderful wondrous side.<br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361069i/711983._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="348" height="348" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><br><em>I received a copy of this book from the author.</em><br><br>No more Jo-etry for a while now, Brownie promise. ;)<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11713419522358838136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_587338509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/587338509" />
    <a title="Basuhi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11758346-basuhi"><img alt="Basuhi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420897928p2/11758346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/587338509?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Basuhi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Basuhi" href="/user/show/11758346-basuhi">Basuhi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Marchetta Lovers and High Fantasy lovers.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11758346-basuhi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587338509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2713754243648431054"><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Book, did you just try to kill me ?</i>
</b><br/><br/>With that epilogue, I swear, you did.<br/><br/>With the <b>
  <i>serrated edges of sorrow</i>
</b> of bidding farewell to Lumatere and Charyn. <br/><br/>With the <b>
  <i>indelible silence of completion.</i>
</b><br/><br/>That is fraught with <b>
  <i>joy so consummating</i>
</b> that it aches.<br/><br/><br/>I guess I got carried away, but that happened because I loved this book. I don't know if I was expecting any different but I still feel that it has surprised me.<br/><br/>I must tell you that this review is going to be long, because I have so much </span>
  <span id="freeText2713754243648431054" style="display:none"><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Book, did you just try to kill me ?</i>
</b><br /><br />With that epilogue, I swear, you did.<br /><br />With the <b>
  <i>serrated edges of sorrow</i>
</b> of bidding farewell to Lumatere and Charyn. <br /><br />With the <b>
  <i>indelible silence of completion.</i>
</b><br /><br />That is fraught with <b>
  <i>joy so consummating</i>
</b> that it aches.<br /><br /><br />I guess I got carried away, but that happened because I loved this book. I don't know if I was expecting any different but I still feel that it has surprised me.<br /><br />I must tell you that this review is going to be long, because I have so much to say and no one to say to. <i>This is my reprieve and this is my closure to the Lumatere chronicles. </i>And I may inadvertently switch to my poetic idiosyncrasies, so.<br /><br /><i>I want to dissect every word of this book and present it to you. With it's beauty and with it's innate significance. How every sentence, every chapter is the quintessence of the whole. How every character is a being you come to love, love with their flaws and their weaknesses. Love like it means to love. And I will try to do that. </i><br /><br />The fact is that I started loving this book because of it's characters.<br /><br />Because it made me love every one of the characters. Maybe love is not quite the right word, passionate is more like it. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Froi</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>The little Sarnak thief.<br />Froi of the exiles.<br />The Lumateran.<br />The flatlands lad.<br />The Charynite.<br />Dafar of Abroi.<br />Froi.</i><br /><br />When I first met Froi, I wouldn't have thought in a million years that I'd be saying this,<br />But I love you, Froi.<br />That was the only thing in my mind as I was reading the last page of this book.<br /><br /><i>He feels everything with an ardor that it entrances you.<br />With a mesmerizing clarity of emotions that it unnerves you.</i><br /><br />In the second book, I wanted to feel sorry for him but I know he doesn't want me to. One might be wondering why I'd feel sorry for someone who was heinous in the first book and tried to rape Evanjalin. Because, there's forgiveness on the victim's part and guilt on the perpetuator's.<br />The easiest way might have been to forget this past of his and never mention of it. But that didn't happen.<br />And I appreciate that.<br /><br />Froi's tenuous relationship with his parents is awkward. <br />And Lovely. Yes, together.<br />I craved his easy charm with Finnikin and Isaboe and his loyal mien with Trevanion or Perri. But there was something bewitching about the gossamer path he trudged with his parents. <br />Like he was in his own elements.<br /><br />And every time, Now that I think of him, it's like I want to weep. <br />With happiness ?<br />Maybe.<br />Because I'll miss him.<br />Yes, I will.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Quintana </b>
</i><br /><br /><i>Quintana of Charyn.<br />She has forgotten what trust is.<br />Forgotten what means to be loved.<br />Lost and insecure and frightened is what she is.<br />Hauteur and arrogance and insolence is what she bares. <br />A madwoman, a fierce savage beauty.<br />Quintana the useless and the hopeless.<br />Quintana the brave, the lovely and the little King's mother.</i><br /><br />Do you see the cover ? Yes, this one. So, do you like it ? When I saw the cover, I instantly fell in love with it. With the savage girl and the verdant hues. <br />Her gleaming eyes and her haughty countenance. Her honest pain, unmasked and bared.<br />If it's ever been possible, I think that I understood Quintana better after a look at this.<br /><br />Quintana is not one you take to your liking. It's difficult to get to know her because Marchetta has not written her PoV a lot and honestly, I don't think her PoV would help matters.<br /><br />Her early life was a tormenting ordeal that has shaped into the insane raging woman that she is. <br /><br />Unflinchingly brave.<br />Determined.<br />Unapologetic.<br />And wildly ravishing.<br /><br />As much as I didn't feel sympathetic to her predicament, I can feel reality marring the esse of her and believe that she is truly a brilliant character despite or more rather because of everything raw and dark she holds within.<br /><br />At moments I've hated her so much that I've wanted to choke the life out of her and then at others I've wanted to hold her tight and whisper that she's not alone. She makes me feel those emotions that are at the opposite ends of the spectrum. Sometimes, all at once.<br /><br />Now there's one thing misleading about the title of the book, neither is this book all about Quintana, nor is it in her point of view. She's the hope for Charyn. Many things revolve around her but it's not very apparent throughout the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Twins and Lirah, the Serker.</i>
</b><br /><br />There is simply something so hypnotic about the charismatic chaos they share, Arjuro, Gargarin and Lirah that I get lost in them.<br /><i>They share a past, a past of regret, of guilt, of retribution.<br />And of love.</i><br />An unusual love amongst themselves and love for Froi that knows no boundaries.<br /><br />When Froi was with Lirah, Gargarin or Arjuro, I wanted sob with the sheer joy of it. A mother and a son. A father and son. The beloved Uncle and son. After all these years.<br />But when they were all together, I wanted to go numb all over.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Finnikin and Isaboe.</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>The Queen and her Consort.<br />The Ruby Ring.<br /></i><br />I'd be lying now if I said that their saccharine love despite it's cloying order doesn't bring a smile to my face.<br /><br />It's like seeing a childhood friend and listening to them speak about their life now and relating it to the memories of the past.<br />Just like that.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Lucian and Phaedra.</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Lucian of the Monts. <br />Queen's beloved cousin.<br />Finnikin's and Balthazar's beloved friend.<br /><br />....And the Charyn wife he sent away.</i><br /><br />See, what I told you about distinctive characters. Here they are, in all their glory.<br /><br />I liked Phaedra and Lucian's romance because it has the highs and lows, the animosity and the passion and at times, unrequited hilarity too.<br /><br />The book is as much about the other characters as much as it's about the strain between Charyn and Lumatere. On the sidelines there were Trevanion and Beatriss with Vestie and then Perri and Tesadora.<br />I liked them all especially, Tesadora, a strong willed woman who yields to no one. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>The Story.<br />The Amazing Tale of the lost and the living.</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />It is unique. When you say something again and again, it loses it's meaning.<br />But I'll say it again because I want to.<br /><br />Unparalleled.<br />Strange.<br />Different.<br /><br /><i>Unique.</i><br /><br />The story is also virile, as if it has a life of it's own.<br />Because it's raw and potent in everything it bares.<br /><br />Raw in the grief.<br />Raw in the pain.<br />In the anguish and the anger.<br />Raw in the eclectic desires.<br />Raw in it's joy as well.<br /><br />And who can deny the amazing eloquence that pulls you in and never lets go. <br /><br />It's like sadness and happiness are woven so close together that you can't differentiate and you feel them both, at the same time, guilty of feeling them simultaneously.<br /><br />Am I rambling ? <br />I don't know.<br />Do I care ?<br />No.<br /><br />This is highly recommended for High Fantasy lovers known to possess a modicum of patience.<br />Yes, patience is the key to unraveling this finely woven enigma. <br /><br /><blockquote> Blood Sings to Blood.</blockquote><br /><br />But more than that, it's Love and Humanity and Forgiveness that have a tune so melliferous it alleviates grief, despondency and anger and everything scathing there is.<br /><br />And, Beautiful, this book was. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2713754243648431054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_792825191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792825191" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/792825191?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=quit-crying-robin">quit-crying-robin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=o-captain-my-captain">o-captain-my-captain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer792825191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4390155984242405921"><b>Buddy read/reread Starting Dec 29 with my friends over on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> formerly known as the Lumatere Group Read</b><br/><br/>Loved it just as much the 2nd time through. What a great, emotional, beautiful story.<br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/let%20me%20love%20you' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419372565ra/13047642.gif' alt='let me love you photo: Friends Letmeloveyou_zps9a48634c.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><b>Overall Series Rating = 4.75</b><br/><b>Quintana of Charyn = 4.5</b><br/><br/>I will not be able to do justice how much I loved this series, it is impossible. Not all of it is happy and the feelings I felt throughout the series ranged the whole spectrum of emotions. I laughed, cried, got angry, hoped beyond bel</span>
  <span id="freeText4390155984242405921" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read/reread Starting Dec 29 with my friends over on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a> formerly known as the Lumatere Group Read</b><br><br>Loved it just as much the 2nd time through. What a great, emotional, beautiful story.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/let%20me%20love%20you" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419372565ra/13047642.gif" alt="let me love you photo: Friends Letmeloveyou_zps9a48634c.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>Overall Series Rating = 4.75</b><br><b>Quintana of Charyn = 4.5</b><br><br>I will not be able to do justice how much I loved this series, it is impossible. Not all of it is happy and the feelings I felt throughout the series ranged the whole spectrum of emotions. I laughed, cried, got angry, hoped beyond belief and could not set the story down for anything else. If you are a fan of fantasy at all it is a must read. <br><br><b>
  <i>“It is what a man does for strangers that counts more than what he does for his family.”</i>
</b><br><br>It is a beautiful thing when an author takes their story to completion and ties everything together. Not every author seems to be able to do that, some lose their message along the way and never recapture it but Melina Marchette was able to tell the story of two lands, both cursed and the boy that unites them. If there is a message within the story I think that it is this:<br><br><b>
  <i>“And through all the misery, she said that some of us in this lifetime experience a moment of beauty beyond reckoning. I asked her what that was, and she said, "If you're one of the lucky ones, you'll know it when you see it. You'll understand why the gods have made you suffer. Because that moment's reward will make your knees weak and everything you've suffered in life will pale in comparison.”</i>
</b><br><br>Our heroes have been through so much suffering in this tale: A Princess forced to suffer the stigma of being a whore so that the other last born girls of her land would not be touched. Twin brothers separated by a deception and forced to bare the punishment meant for the other. Lovers torn apart for almost two decades and parents separated from their child for nearly as long. And finally Froi connected to all of them in some way saved by the Lumateers and unacknowledged father of the future king growing in the crazy princess Quintana’s belly. Each has a devastating tale but all are also so full of hope for that moment they are willing to trudge through all the struggles to make it happen.<br><br><b>
  <i>“And if the gods were to give me a choice between living a better life, having not met them, or a wretched life with the slightest chance of crossing their path, then I’d pick the wretched life over and over again.”</i>
</b><br><br>At 100 pages into the story I had no idea how Marchetta was going to bring the story together. It was such a tangled weave where everything was in upheaval. But in the end she pulled it off beautifully. She was honest to the characters and while sometimes that made me mad at them, because I just wanted everyone to get along, each character had their own journey to make and their own priorities. <br><br>I really don’t want to give too much away because the story was so well thought out and executed it should really be experienced without any spoilers. But much like Lord of the Rings there are multiple stories going on at once that all have to come together in the end.<br><br>The stories revolving include but are not limited to:<br><br>Quintana is in hiding in the Valley on the boarder of Lumatere and is being helped by Phaedra who most think is dead. She is also stuck with a few other women who would not be the first choice for help in a situation like this but they are along for the ride. Phaedra and Lucian, two people who have finally discovered that they are in love but still torn my duty to their prospective kingdoms/queendoms. Froi who must find an army for Quintana and his babe but find resistance everywhere along the way. Gargarin, Lirah and Arjuro who have the most tragic of pasts and are trying to help Froi build a future for Charyn no matter what future sacrifices they must make for him. Isaboe and Finnikin who need peace for their own kingdom but still have so much hate for Charyn and Quintana. The upcoming war against Bestiano and the army he has acquired in order to get Quintana back on the throne.<br><br>With all of those stories going on I could not walk away from this book. This had some of the most poignant moments in it of any book I’ve read that will stick with me probably forever. The cave scene between Isaboe and Quintana being the one that I think I will always associate with this book. It was heart wrenching, hopeful and showed just how well thought out all of the characters were. How even though the people were from different lands in the ferocity of love for their people they were the same.<br><br>I’m so sad to leave this world. I wanted to stay immersed in it even longer or come back to it in the next generation of characters when Froi and Quintana’s son comes of age to take the throne. This is a series that I’m sure I’ll read again and again. There was something for everyone and it is so hard to walk away at the end.<br><br><br><br>Dec 29 2013<br>My actual review to come but I want this marked as finished before the new year. <br><br>I really want to do this book and the whole series justice in my review and that will take a little more thought as there was so much, so many feels. But all I can say is that if you are a fan of fantasy this is a series that should be on your must read list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4390155984242405921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=covers-i-love">covers-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139578849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10876276494935027684">I think I love you, Melina Marchetta, for making a series/trilogy after the wonderfulness that was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_' title='Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a>.</span>
  <span id="freeText10876276494935027684" style="display:none">I think I love you, Melina Marchetta, for making a series/trilogy after the wonderfulness that was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_296482539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/296482539" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/296482539?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=teary-eyed-reads">teary-eyed-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer296482539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4333063167410250060">Rating: 4.75 Stars <br/><br/>Well, call me a coward, but I have been avoiding writing this review like the plague. Actually, <i>worse, </i>considering I'd run towards a plague before I ran towards writing a review for this. I always have two feelings when I finish a Melina Marchetta novel. One, of being incredible happy, content, and simply awe-struck for the novel is always amazing beyong belief; and second, of feeling ever-so-slightly nervous because, let's be honest, how could I <i>ever</i> possibly even <i>think</i> or <i>im</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4333063167410250060" style="display:none">Rating: 4.75 Stars <br /><br />Well, call me a coward, but I have been avoiding writing this review like the plague. Actually, <i>worse, </i>considering I'd run towards a plague before I ran towards writing a review for this. I always have two feelings when I finish a Melina Marchetta novel. One, of being incredible happy, content, and simply awe-struck for the novel is always amazing beyong belief; and second, of feeling ever-so-slightly nervous because, let's be honest, how could I <i>ever</i> possibly even <i>think</i> or <i>imagine</i> how to write a review that would do the book I read justice of <i>any</i> kind? Well, I can't. What I <i>can</i> do, however, is tell you that I loved <em>Quintana of Charyn.</em> It is a beautiful, provocative, and gorgeously written novel that ties up all loose ends, concludes this series without flaws, and renders me speechless. <em>Yet,</em> for the first time, I have to admit that there is something about this book that fell just a tiiiny bit flat for me. I feel like a traitor saying this, especially considering I've given every single one of Marchetta's novels 5 Stars and even went out of my way to order this novel from Australia because I couldn't <i>wait</i> to read it and it was only releasing in America around six-ish months later, <i>but,</i> when compared to all of Marchetta's prior works, I feel as if this just might have been her weakest novel yet.<br /><br />When I began <em>Quintana of Charyn,</em> I thought for sure that it would wind up being my favorite of the Lumatere Chronicles. Well, <em>Finnikin of the Rock</em> still is, although I suspect <em>Froi of the Exiles</em> would be if I re-read it, knowing all that I do now about Quintana's character. Nevertheless, somewhere a little after the half-way mark of this story, <i>Quintana</i> began to steadily lose me. It wasn't that the story lagged or that I was bored, it was simply that it was <em>too</em> overly dramatic. I didn't need <em>that</em> many scenes or <em>that</em> much build-up and prolongment to the happy ending we all knew was awaiting us. I found myself wondering why so many pages were still left when not so much of the actual story was left at all. It was a very well-written conclusion that brought a smile to my face, but the fact that it fell into the let-me-be-a-dramatic-conclusion trope was rather disappointing.<br /><br />Nevertheless, <em>Quintana of Charyn</em>
   is simply breathtaking. Marchetta has a gift for weaving together multiple story lines and the gradual manner in which the lives of Finnikin, Froi, Isaboe, Lucien, Phaedra, and Quintana herself all came to be together, 
intertwined
   and 
interlapped
   with one another, was truly beautiful. It is evident, with every novel that she writes, that Marchetta takes on astounding themes and valuable life lessons, but perhaps what I loved the most about <i>Quintana</i> especially was just how <i>real</i> everything felt. We often go through life and reach points where everything seems to fit together like a puzzle piece; we realize that things all happened for a reason and that reason was to bring us to <i>this point.</i> Well, reading this novel is a little like that too. It never feels forced or rushed, but all flows so naturally that it's easy to forget you're reading about people who aren't real, who aren't there in front of your eyes, whose suffering isn't your own because it certainly feels that way.<br /><br />Another one of the best things about this novel was its heavy emphasis on friendship and the growth that each of the characters experienced, despite the fact that we had met them before and seen them grow before; like humans, they still had a long way to go in their lives and were never finished fully growing after all. Isaboe and Finnikin, for example, are the characters we've known the longest, but the turns their relationship took, the hurdles they still had to cross, were so very realistically drawn-up and handled. Quintana, too, faced immense change as she formed bonds of friendship with Phaedra and the other Charynites in the Lumaterean valley. Theirs was a friendship reminiscent of that from <i>Saving Francesca,</i> my favorite Marchetta novel to date, and their gradual trust and understanding of one another moved me beyond words. Yet, it was the story of Phaedra of Alonso that tugged the most at my heartstrings. Phaedra is a character that is easy to overlook for she isn't in-your-face courageous like Isaboe and she isn't strange-but-beautiful like Quintana. Instead, her strength lies within, in her resolve and belief and faith in others. It is easy to paint her in the picture of a saint, but her inner struggles and the constant hurdles that she faced and even the times when even <i>she</i> seemed to lose hope only added to the realistic quality behind this story and the whirlwind of emotion that came with it.<br /><br />Moreover, Lucien and Phaedra's relationship is, without a doubt, my favorite of all the young couples in this series. Although Finnikin is my sweetheart, I couldn't keep the helplessly wide and cheesy grin from my face whenever Phaedra and Lucien interacted, or just whenever Lucien made an appearance. Note, however, that I said <i>young</i> couples. You see, my favorite couple in the entire novel is the one between Gargarin of Abroi and his wife, the beautiful Lirah. For some reason, seeing couples who have weathered storms and still managed to stay together, acting so sweetly even after having children and as they age, always yanks my heart in weird directions. Furthermore, this may have something to do with the fact that Gargarin, with his (admit it) social awkwardness at times, his scholarly role, his shyness at admitting his true feelings for anyone, his (rather) pessimistic thoughts, and yet his deep, <i>deep</i> depth of feeling for his family, is somehow one of my favorite characters of all time, perhaps because he tends to remind me of myself at times. It is Gargarin's story line, with the flurry of feeling that he holds for his twin brother, that broke my heart a million times over in this novel. Truly, these brothers never cease to amaze me.<br /><br />Froi too, whose life is intertwined so closely with Gargarin's, is a character that continues to astound me with every novel, especially due to his rocky relationship with his parents and
  
     his constant inner struggle between his Charynite and Lumaterean selves. I love how Marchetta explores dedication to ones nation, ones Gods, and ones faith. It's all so beautifully intertwined that I can't even describe it properly only to say that it brought me to tears on so many occasions. It is evident that Marchetta knows what it feels like to be an immigrant, an exile in ones own nation, and she captures this paradoxical ideal perfectly. While I did feel as if the amount of Froi and Quintana time was significantly lower than that of any other couple in this novel, I enjoyed seeing Froi's affection grow with distance and see his bonds with his family finally come to a full, blooming, and caring circle.<br /><br />Melina Marchetta is an author I can count on to bring me to tears, to make me just lay there on my bed, thinking for hours on end every time I finish her books, and 
  
  <em>Quintana of Charyn</em>
  
     definitely did not disappoint. It may not be my favorite novel of hers, but it is a memorable one nevertheless. It's one that won't stray too far from my thoughts for the messages this series extols about love, patience, hope, faith, belief, and friendship. Now, looking back on this series as a whole, I can truly admit that everything has come around in a full circle and Marchetta continues to render me speechless with the beauty of her work. If it isn't evident already, here is a woman who can <i>write,</i> who can <i>capture</i> emotion, who can <i>convey</i> belief, and who has managed to take on one of the toughest, most complex and intriguing series I've come across and truly <i>make it work.</i> If this isn't a testament of Marchetta's skill, then I don't know what is. All I can do now is wait for the <i>Jellicoe Road</i> film that is currently under production and keep my fingers crossed for another Marchetta novel soon, because I simply cannot get enough of this writing...this beauty.<br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/12/review-quintana-of-charyn-lumatere.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> 
  
</span>
  <a data-text-id="4333063167410250060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer914342264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5663496786163436320"><b>
  <u>
    <i>SPOILERS FOR FROI OF THE EXILES</i>
  </u>
</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>4.5 STARS<br/><blockquote>”Do you love me?” he asked instead. “because if you don’t, I’d wait until you did. I’d wait weeks and months and years.”</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>I fell in love with that line without knowing who said them or the context of those words. <br/><br/>This was such a breathtaking reminder on why I read books.<br/><br/>Because in the culture fostered here in Goodreads, underneath the insurmountable TBR pile, the endless galleys that you burden yourself to review before their release day… it’</span>
  <span id="freeText5663496786163436320" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>
    <i>SPOILERS FOR FROI OF THE EXILES</i>
  </u>
</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>4.5 STARS<br /><blockquote>”Do you love me?” he asked instead. “because if you don’t, I’d wait until you did. I’d wait weeks and months and years.”</blockquote></b>
</i><br />I fell in love with that line without knowing who said them or the context of those words. <br /><br />This was such a breathtaking reminder on why I read books.<br /><br />Because in the culture fostered here in Goodreads, underneath the insurmountable TBR pile, the endless galleys that you burden yourself to review before their release day… it’s so easy to lose sight of that. It becomes easy to nitpick and cry stereotype at the slightest clue, critique the geo-cultural soundness of world building in high fantasy and almost reflexive to completely write-off a story that makes use of rape as a plot device. It’s like picking a string, any string to pull and you can ruin a well-crafted book for yourself.<br /><br /><i>Quintana of Charyn</i> made it difficult for me to fall back on those patterns, seeing as how it treads in the side of wonders.<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>There’s a babe in my belly that whispers the valley, Froi.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />The prologue starts with Quintana speaking to Froi, coming from a place that was completely out of left field. Froi, on the other hand, is with Arjuro in Sebastabol having separated form Quintana after Olivier’s betrayal outside Paladozza at the end of <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>. Isaboe is with child, sending her best men and her consort Finnikin to intercept Gargarin of Abroi, the former first advisor to the Charynite king and suspected of being the hand responsible for the death of her family. Lucian, and the Monts join the Charynnites in the mourning of the death of his wife, Phaedra and their women. Together with the oppressive presence of the Street Lords of Citavita, the desertion of the <i>provincari</i> of Alonso and the refusal of Isaboe to provide for them, the valley seems as desolate and abandoned as ever.<br /><br />Confession: I purposely delayed reading this trilogy (which really felt like a duology to me, by the way) for more than one reasons. Having been introduced to Marchetta’s oeuvre through her contemporary work, there’s an element to her writing that makes me wary of putting that in the context of high fantasy. She doesn’t give her story easily. It takes a bit of patience and more focus than I’d usually give in fiction. Meshing that with building a world from ground up I thought would drive me up against the wall. Also the fangirling over this series was just too extreme! I might lose friends over this admission but the harder you push me to read a book with incessant gushing and fawning, the more I delay reading it.<br /><br /><i>Quintana of Charyn</i> made me eat all of my assumptions and more.<br /><br />In more ways than one, it was the reward at the end of all that tedium. All that incessant traveling, characters whose backstories you can’t seem to care about as much as you want (i.e. Lirah, Gargarin and Arjuro). It felt a lot like you’re left to marinade with all those ingredients for a good long while, simmering in low heat so that it permeates through your skin, down to the bones, until its part of who you are. This is the book where you get thrown into the fire and come out repurposed and recalibrated…<br /><br />Annnnd… I just made myself hungry.<br /><br />Remember that John Green quote about <i>Imperial Affliction</i>? How there are books that make you want to violently push down everyone’s throats and there are books that make advertising what you feel about them seem like a betrayal of sorts? This was neither for me. It’s not my <i>Imperial Affliction</i> yet I also refuse to embarrass it with my juvenile gushing and platitudes. But it did change me as a reader. <br /><br />What I liked most about this series was that Marchetta illustrated it best how to believably redeem a character without insulting her readers’ intelligence. The fact that the focus of the series shifts from Finnkin and Isaboe to a character as deplorable as Froi may be a prime deterrent for some. But in the hands of this author, that single act of depravity was never forgotten, both by Froi and the reader, evolving believably as a part of the character as the story progressed. It was never really an issue with me to begin with, never felt it as a gratuitous plot device and always considered it a poor excuse for giving up on this story. This series honours you with the expectation that you are a thinking reader and it deserves to be honoured back by one’s open heart and non-judgmental mind.<br /><br />I love the way this made me fall in love with every single character. This was told in multiple POVs with Quintana the sole character given the first person perspective when she speaks to Froi in her mind. The way I am made to care about the backstory of supporting characters such as Tessadora and Perri by viewing their relationship through the eyes of Lucian or Isaboe was brilliant in its plight to make me sympathetic for everyone. Quintana was a revelation in this book, one that will stand apart from every strong heroine stereotype I’ll be coming across from hereon out. Dancing, crooked teeth notwithstanding.<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>”Our spirit is mightier than the filth of our memories, Florenza of Nebia. remember that or you’ll be vomiting for the rest of your life.”<br />Florenza stared up at Quintana, and something passed between them as she nodded solemnly and wiped her mouth with the back of her hand.<br />“And Tippideaux of Paladozza, the provincaro De Lancey’s daughter, has the prettiest face in Charyn,” she continued to inform them all. “Not you. So don’t believe a word your mother says.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />She probably had the best lines form this book and four out of five of them are the most epic burns.<br /><br />Apart from the impossibility of making Quintana fully-formed in my mind this time around, this book also made me love Phaedra and Lucian even more. To the point that I wanted to take one star away from this for not giving them the main story instead. I felt emotionally disconnected with Lirah, Arjuro and Gargarin’s side of the story in <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> only to be sent sobbing repeatedly whenever they turn up in this book. <br /><br />And no, I am not the sort of reader who sobs.<br /><br />The series all throughout was rooted in multiple conflicts among the richly detailed history of its characters: mothers, fathers and sons, husband and wives, brothers and sisters, survivors and oppressors, a queen to another queen and so on and so forth. And within each of these characters lie the complexities behind a traitor, of the motivations behind a deserting mother and the rhyme and reason behind hatred and forgiveness without force-feeding the sentiments. You just willingly fall for each and every one of them.<br /><br /> Outside this book, with the sheer volume of subplots, neglecting one or the other seems an inevitability. It’s often a conundrum you feel in high fantasy: choosing between the characters and the world building, their motivations, their sorrows and their joys versus the politics, the socio-cultural issues and making it relatable to current realities. This story was generous in both counts, the relationships fully-embodied and emphatic, making you clutch desperately to stay in this world just a while longer as you reach the end, wanting to know what becomes of Rafuel or Olivier… or Jasmina and Tariq.<br /><br />It wasn’t perfect for me. It nearly was but despite the blitz of the overwhelming feels, the many new beloved characters that fills very crevice of my heart and the niggling desperation not to see it end yet, I found it a bit of a stretch for me to buy into the whole conflict between Froi and Quintana versus the <i>provincati</i>. After all that has happened, I thought as an entity, Charyn’s <i>provincati</i> failed to cut across the gravity of their worth in the story.<br /><br />A small imperfection that I almost missed from having my eyes constantly blurred by tears.<br /><br />I’ve gone on too long yet again! It’s always the best ones that reduces me to a babbling, incoherent fool and I will hate this review soon as I put it up. Days will pass, other books will be read, stars will be handed out and the details of The Lumatere Chronicles will not be as clear to me as it is today… but no, outside of that, not to be dramatic, but nothing will be the same in the after for me.<br /><br /><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/881702/mother-fucking-onions-" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on Booklikes.</a><br />==========<br /><br /><b>MOTHER. FUCKING. ONIONS.</b><br /><br />Felt like I was chopping a barrel full of them getting through this.<br /><br />How do you say "I love you" in Marchetta?<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Step away,” he whispered. “If you step away I’ll learn from you. I’ll find the desire in me to live without you. Much the same as you want to live without me.”<br />“I didn’t say I wanted to live without you,” she said, angry tears springing in her eyes. “Only that I can. I’ve practiced. I’ve been very good in that way.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />I am going to review this. Somehow. Once I can.<br /><br />Fucking onions....</span>
  <a data-text-id="5663496786163436320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319666686p2/4222084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238066035?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie">Maggie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=aussie-aussie-aussie-oi-oi-oi">aussie-aussie-aussie-oi-oi-oi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=dawson-leery-cried">dawson-leery-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=crushworthy-guys">crushworthy-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you">i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=frenzied-anticipation">frenzied-anticipation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=aussie-2012">aussie-2012</a>
