        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238066035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6698013561301748078">What can I say about this book but faith rewarded? How do I begin to talk about a series that turned me onto a new genre?<br/><br/>Marchetta took me on a journey through an unfamiliar genre and story landscape, through curses and the Citavita. Looking back on <b>Finnikin</b>, I couldn't even finish <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203351167' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review</a> because I was so unused to fantasy. I was exhausted by the little I did manage to write. By the time I read <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207570644' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi</a>
</b>, I was better prepared and any exhaustion I felt was due to the emotional ride from the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText6698013561301748078" style="display:none">What can I say about this book but faith rewarded? How do I begin to talk about a series that turned me onto a new genre?<br /><br />Marchetta took me on a journey through an unfamiliar genre and story landscape, through curses and the Citavita. Looking back on <b>Finnikin</b>, I couldn't even finish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203351167" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> because I was so unused to fantasy. I was exhausted by the little I did manage to write. By the time I read <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207570644" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi</a>
</b>, I was better prepared and any exhaustion I felt was due to the emotional ride from the book.<br /><br />With <b>Quintana</b>, I could talk about how Lucian and Perri should star in their own buddy cop show, or how being in Quintana's head seemed like the most natural place to be. I loved so many of the characters, but for me, this series comes down to two people -- Isaboe and Froi. The things that bond them are at the heart of the series. They are the faces of children of war.<br /><br />In Isaboe, we see what war does to a once beloved, sheltered child. Her experiences in Sarnak and Sorel shape the fierce queen she’s become. She’s unflinching. However, sometimes that results in a harshness that had me wincing. It's how she survived on her own, but it may not be the best way to ensure her people's survival.<br /><br />For Froi, it was Sir Topher who prevented him from going down an irreversible path, but that and a belief in a girl with magic, shaped the man he became. His journey of redemption -- never once forgetting what could have been -- is about overcoming all the experiences that can break you and turn you into someone you're not. I loved seeing the person Froi came to be when given love and when he gave his love in return. It was so wholehearted and pure. It was devastating to think what war did to the boy with that much heart.<br /><br />One character I didn't feel much affection for was Lady Zarah. To quote the great Dionne Warwick, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lF6jR44RCwc" rel="nofollow noopener">I got your number, hussy</a>!<br /><br /><b>Quintana of Charyn</b> tested the bounds of loyalty, friendship, and family, and what it meant to be Lumateran, Charynite, Queen, husband, wife, lover, and friend. It's about having faith first, like a boy with cats once did, so it can be rewarded later. I loved being in this world and I hope Marchetta revisits it again, as I know I will.<br /><br /><b>Rating: 5/5 stars.</b><br /><br />I leave the <a href="http://youngadultanonymous.blogspot.com/2012/11/yaa-soundtrack-lumatere-boxset.html" rel="nofollow noopener">playlist-making to Noelle</a>, but one song that played over and over in my head while reading Quintana was <a href="http://youtu.be/7TupvVpxY_U" rel="nofollow noopener">This Woman's Work by Kate Bush</a>.<br /><br /><br /><i>This review appears on <a href="http://youngadultanonymous.blogspot.com/2012/11/review-quintana-of-charyn-by-melina.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Anonymous</a>, along with Part One of the <a href="http://youngadultanonymous.blogspot.com/2012/11/yaa-soundtrack-lumatere-boxset.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Lumatere Boxset</a>.</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_302819878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302819878" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302819878?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302819878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3405585253188871858">Melina Marchetta's <i>Lumatere Chronicles</i> is like the crowning jewel of the young adult fantasy genre, so of course I had huge expectations coming into <i>Quintana of Charyn</i>. Twice now, Marchetta has delivered indescribable stories of a cursed land, a nation of refugees, a series of powerful characters who exemplified hope, vengeance, and forgiveness rising from great tragedy, all through two unforgettable books. And with so much on the line, a lot can go wrong, but I’m happy to report every word is w</span>
  <span id="freeText3405585253188871858" style="display:none">Melina Marchetta's <i>Lumatere Chronicles</i> is like the crowning jewel of the young adult fantasy genre, so of course I had huge expectations coming into <i>Quintana of Charyn</i>. Twice now, Marchetta has delivered indescribable stories of a cursed land, a nation of refugees, a series of powerful characters who exemplified hope, vengeance, and forgiveness rising from great tragedy, all through two unforgettable books. And with so much on the line, a lot can go wrong, but I’m happy to report every word is well worth the wait, <i>Quintana of Charyn</i> ends the series on a high note.<br /><br />I don’t think I need to recap how much I enjoyed <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>, a book so moving I didn’t think it could be topped - until I read <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>. By now, every one of these characters, Froi, Finnikin, Isaboe, Quintana, Lucian, Phaedra, and so many others, are like familiar friends, and many a scene in <i>Quintana of Charyn</i> brought a smile to my face simply by reminding me of how much I’ve grown to care for each of them, their friendships, their families, their loyalties, their struggles, their triumphs. And <i>Quintana </i> really brings this series full circle - with her attention to detail, her gift for subtle character development, and her ability to make even minor events of the first book hugely relevant to the current plot, Marchetta’s done a wonderful job tying together the three books in some really neat yet intricate ways. In a way, it’s fitting too, because <i>Quintana of Charyn</i> is a fairly straightforward story, the plot does an admirable but relatively simple job of connecting the futures of its characters with the fate of Charyn, just like <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> connected the futures of the characters of that book with the fate of Lumatere - I’d definitely say this final book is stylistically closer to the first than its direct predecessor. For me, <i>Quintana</i> never approaches the sheer complexity of <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>, but it doesn’t have to, <i>Froi</i> already does the required work by setting up these wonderfully complex characters, and all <i>Quintana</i> has to do is bring them home.<br /><br />Of course, it’s not that easy, going home. Even though the title of the book is <i>Quintana of Charyn</i>, plotwise it’s really <i>Froi of the Exiles, Part Two</i>, because the focus of the story is still Froi’s journey. He’s torn between his home with the Lumaterans and his home with Quintana, Gargarin, Arjuro, and Lirah in Charyn, and his conflict over where he belongs, like an extension of the wider conflict between Lumatere and Charyn - but on a personal level, just resonates throughout the book. It’s incredible how effortlessly Marchetta’s writing seems to emphasize all these conflicting ties in one person, with Froi’s loyalty and friendship with Finnikin and Isaboe balanced perfectly against his love for Quintana, Gargarin, and Lirah. So no matter where Froi happened to be, no matter what he happened to do, I was always rooting for him to find his place in the world, even though both sides are written so pitch perfectly I couldn’t even decide myself how he should choose, that’s how powerfully every single one of Froi’s relationships feels. I’m not going to spoil the ending, but the way it’s resolved, it’s one of the most appropriate endings I’ve ever read, and it just kept reminding me of <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>’s most memorable line, ‘<i>blood sings to blood</i>’.<br /><br />But even if the focus is on Froi, so many other stories, Finnikin’s, Isaboe’s, Phaedra’s, Quintana’s, they all seamlessly intersect to combine into one incredible book. Quintana made such a huge impression on me in <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> with her tragic character and strange demeanor, and here she demonstrates once again how she’s much more than just Froi’s other half. In hiding, she’s got a lot to do, building slow, inspiring friendships with Phaedra in particular but also with a couple of other strong female characters, demonstrating just how tough she is, heck, opening not just my eyes, but the eyes of her fellow Charynites. I always looked forward to the few sections from her point of view, there’s a certain strange poetry to her tortured words, but even from the point of view of any of the other characters, she shows why she deserves to headline this book even if the story is ultimately about Froi. A quick read of just the epilogue alone reveals just how far she’s come as a character, not just from the tragedy surrounding her birth and childhood, but from Charyn’s entire history. Hers is the kind of ending that leaves me hopeful for the future.<br /><br />Of course, even if Froi and Quintana are obviously the two main characters, their stories are just the tip of the iceberg. <i>Quintana of Charyn</i> is such a fully character driven novel, I can spend days covering every single character who made an impression on me and I still wouldn’t be finished. Isaboe and Finnikin, sure, Finnikin annoyed me at first with his overpossessiveness, but I meant it when I said Finnikin’s friendship with Froi, like so much of the book, shines through in a way that brought a smile to my face. Isaboe even more, not just her obvious love for Finnikin, but the incredible way her character develops through the book, shedding her stoic Evanjalin guise to reveal a far more multifaceted character, someone deeply hurt by the events of Lumatere’s recent past but, in the end, is still a big enough person that she’s capable of demonstrating just how powerful small gestures can be. Or Phaedra and Lucian, their story was kind of out of place in <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> but <i>Quintana</i> ties their plotline with the main story so well, and yet somehow still manages to retain everything that made it special, their mutual respect for each others’ strengths, the emotion in Phaedra’s sacrifice. And I haven’t even talked about Gargarin and Arjuro and Lirah and Tesadora and De Lancey and Beatriss and Barakah and Lord August and Perri and Olivier and Dorcas and even Celie who makes an appearance from <i>Ferragost</i>, truly, I am going to miss every single one of these characters.<br /><br />So, I have good news and I have bad news. Good news, <i>Quintana of Charyn</i> is a wholly character driven fantasy that shattered all of my expectations for the final book of the <i>Lumatere Chronicles</i>. Bad news, this may be the final book by Melina Marchetta for some time. But if, like Gargarin, I look on the side of wonder, her hiatus really only reinforces my appreciation for how truly special this series has been.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3405585253188871858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer317536614" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17171654333865386169"><b>Final rating: 6/5 stars</b><br/><br/>This was.....fantastic. At least for me. I always loved Lumatere, especially after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a>, which was NOT what i expected of young adult fantasy to be. Great job Melina, great job!<br/><br/>This book was so wonderful, I just didn't want to put it down. Every sentence was beautiful and her writing style is amazing. <br/><br/>I am very, very sad to see that this is how it ends. There are those times where I love to read long series (more than 3 books) and when I don't. This series fa</span>
  <span id="freeText17171654333865386169" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 6/5 stars</b><br><br>This was.....fantastic. At least for me. I always loved Lumatere, especially after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>, which was NOT what i expected of young adult fantasy to be. Great job Melina, great job!<br><br>This book was so wonderful, I just didn't want to put it down. Every sentence was beautiful and her writing style is amazing. <br><br>I am very, very sad to see that this is how it ends. There are those times where I love to read long series (more than 3 books) and when I don't. This series falls into: <i> why you not longer, you make me sad </i> category. <br><br>The whole time while i was reading it, I had no idea how it would end. <br><br>Anyway, this was really interesting, because i had no idea how it would end. Anyways, there were many things that made me shocked, there were times when i cursed the villain and times when my eyes filled with tears.<br>Soooo.........<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375843i/730509.jpg" width="500" height="370" alt="Damn you Froi, why u not real" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> As for the ending:</b> It ended really satisfying, and i screamed in happiness because I was glad this turned out to be series with a strong ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was so happy for Froi and Quin ♥ I always loved them, and thank god they got their happy ending. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b> MY LUMATERE CHRONICLES REVIEWS: </b><br><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536501" rel="nofollow noopener"> Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) </a> <br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536566" rel="nofollow noopener"> Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) </a> <br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536614" rel="nofollow noopener"> Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) </a> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_279636111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279636111" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279636111?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=rereading-material">rereading-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-approved">male-approved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=aussie-and-nz">aussie-and-nz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=once-upon-a-time">once-upon-a-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279636111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7089627358156790727">———— 2019<br/><br/>I can’t measure the worth of this book (this entire story) in number of stars. <br/>Entire constellations would never be enough. <br/>The known universe might not make it justice. <br/><br/>All that I know is... the endless love I hold for these characters, the deep respect for the brilliant author, the sorrow and happiness that followed me throughout the story, the intricately woven plot twists by which I was left aghast and teary-eyed, the satisfying sigh I gave at the end. My heart never stood a chance,</span>
  <span id="freeText7089627358156790727" style="display:none">———— 2019<br><br>I can’t measure the worth of this book (this entire story) in number of stars. <br>Entire constellations would never be enough. <br>The known universe might not make it justice. <br><br>All that I know is... the endless love I hold for these characters, the deep respect for the brilliant author, the sorrow and happiness that followed me throughout the story, the intricately woven plot twists by which I was left aghast and teary-eyed, the satisfying sigh I gave at the end. My heart never stood a chance, it fell in love over and over again, from the first page to the very last. <br><br>How does one measure that? <br><br><i>“[...] today, I think I’m leaning on the side of wonder”</i> and I have no idea what you’re reading, but I hope it’s just as spectacular as this series is to me! <br><br>———— 2012<br><br><i>If there is a book that I can read with my eyes filled with tears and my heart full of happiness, it is one of Marchetta's stories..</i><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-quintana-of-charyn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370144i/722919.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>FULL REVIEW:</b><br><br>This story took my breath away!<br>It's an ocean of emotions that I've been sinking in and it's not like I haven't expected it, because I really did. I knew it was coming and even thought I was prepared for the force of it, it still blew my mind away - I loved it from the first page to the very last one .. and I guess my love for it will still go on forever.<br><br>Be warned, this is what this series might do to you: it might drown you while you try to breathe in all the beauty of this world and with every word you'll only want more and more; oh, such a wonderful addiction that will leave you breathless, speechless, crying and smiling all in the same time.<br><br>There is no one in this world (and I really mean NO ONE) that could write like Melina Marchetta. I hope that she already knows what an amazing writer she is, because if there is a book that I can read with my eyes filled with tears and my heart full of happiness, it is one of her stories.. Her words 'sing' to us and we can hear them from all around the world.<br><br>I loved with all my heart the first two books in this series and this ending (Quintana of Charyn) was all that I've expected and then much more.<br>This is a powerful story that still burns into my soul; it's like a symphony of joy, sorrow, fear, hate, love.. and hope (above them all there is hope, because this is the only gift she can give to her characters after all the suffering they've endured for all those years).<br><br>As usual with Marcheta's books I am somehow at a loss for words.<br>How can I describe its beauty if I can barely gasp it all?<br>My husband asked me to tell him about it, and I didn't even know where to start. Everything seems important to me, every character has a voice and a destiny worth telling, every scene made my heart ache for joy or for sorrow..<br><br>I could never make justice to this book, to this fantastic world. Because this was such a complex story (the whole series is) with so many destinies to follow, with so many entwined lives, with so many turnarounds, with so many wonderful or terrible scenes, with so many tears to shed, with so many cries of emotion.. There is so much beauty in the writing and the world building that it hurts.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-quintana-of-charyn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370144i/722920.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is not only a story about Quintana (not even a story about only Quintana and Froi).<br>It is a story about Charyn and Lumatere, a story about 2 queens, about two curses, about a cave with 5 completely different women trying to protect the truth and the future of a kingdom. This is a story about a man and his parents on their race to safe the unsavable, a story about a king that is to be born and give hope to a world of dispair.. This is a story about friendship, and trust, and forgiveness, and hope. It's full of death, of blood, of tears, but also full of life and joy and smiles..<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>But she stepped forward and placed a finger to his lips and there it was before him. The greatest prayer to the gods he could muster with a heart so broken. "Don't let me outlive this woman. Don't let me exist one moment without her".</i>
</blockquote><br><b>So this is goodbye...</b><br>It's becoming a habit - me saying goodbye to a series I love, with my hands trembling and my vision blurred.. And here's what I'll miss from Lumatere and Charyn:<br><br>- I'll miss Isaboe and Finnikin, their strength, the beauty of their hearts, the love for each other and their people, their happiness shared with their friends and their daughter.<br>- I'll miss Finn's father (Trevanion) and his family (Beatrice and Vestie) - even though we didn't see much of them in this book, I will always hold them close to my heart.<br>- I'll miss Lucian and Phaedra, the valley, the people they cared and protected, I'll miss Tesadora and Perri... I'll miss Lumatere as a whole - with the dark and the light, with the dreams and the horrors, and everything in between.<br>- And also, it hurts to say goodbye to Froi and Quintana and their family. There was so much pain in their lives, there was so much suffering in being apart from each other, but their love was strong and I won't forget their story, nor will I ever forget the twins (Gargarin and Arjuro) or the beautiful Lirah. It's been a long, long way full of deceit and pain and struggle, so I wish them all the happiness in the world and a very bright future to warm their hearts.. And my wish is not only for them, but for all the friends they have, for all the people that helped them, for all the people that survived the curse and fought for its breaking.<br><br>And there is more: three books filled with reasons to love, hundreds of pages to steal your heart and break it and put it back together only to break it one once more... And even <strong>
  <em>then</em>
</strong> there might be more...<br><br><strong>Minnor spoilers:</strong><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I want to remember how the relation between Isaboe and Quintana got to change; how Phaedra got to be close to both queens and how she found a way back in Lucian's life; how Finn found Froi and how all the stories overlapped; how all the women in the cave got past their hate and misstrust in order to protect their Queen.. I want to remember the love our sweet couples shared and I want to remember the tragedy, the curses that bound two kingdoms, the song that called their people home, I want to remember the beauty and the horror, the happiness and the despair, I want to keep them all in my heart and never let them go. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>A book will be closed as others will be opened...<br>... may all Marcetta's future books be as good as this series, because we really couldn't ask for more.<br><br>Happy midnight dreaming!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-quintana-of-charyn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696540.jpg" alt="" width="483" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> * This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-quintana-of-charyn.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br><br>————————————————————————————<br><br>NOTES:<br><br>Re-read June 2013 - I might write soon a new review for the series, as it blew my mind once more and I still love it to pieces. Just know that this is a heartbreaking story that I will always hold close to my heart. Absolutely fabulous!!!<br><br>———— 2019<br><br>PS: I noticed <i>at least</i> 3 new open doors (I'm not saying that the author will come back to this world, it's just an observation I made during my re-readings - and of course I wouldn't mind it one bit if she DID write some more) with the repeated wonder of the open ocean, the Yutlind South matter, and the talk (between Finn, his queen &amp; the priest) about who else is marked for a meaningful path. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was only one very tiny thing that bugged me a bit. <br>I understand the need to secure the borders (now that Charyn was united and seemed to be more powerful than ever) and that giving away land was more for the sake of the future of Lumatere and less for Froi, but I wanted the negotiations to have taken a different turn. For one, I don't see Isaboe giving land to the charynites, not one centimetre, probably not even over her dead body; and there is also the way it happened like an afterthought, not a decision made by the queen or even the consort. This is not mentioned outside those few lines, but it sits wrong on my mind each time I read the book. <br><br>Other than this, the story is pure perfection from the first word to the last and my love for it is endless!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>————————————————<br><br>Before reading:<br>I swear time is standing still or going backwards *sigh*<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370144i/722921.jpg" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>October, please come faster.. Pretty please!<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/823060075?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz* Fashionably Late" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz* Fashionably Late" href="/user/show/8191214-liz-fashionably-late">Liz* Fashionably Late</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Marchetta's groupies</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=le-feels">le-feels</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer823060075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17128674567628250478">Reading a Marchetta, always:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/657526.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>_______________<br/>Re-read 2020 under quarantine. Just as perfect as the first time.<br/> <br/><b>...leaning on the side of wonder.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390329968ra/8192424.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390329968ra/8192425.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm genuinely moved by this series, I really am. I'm not good with words, I'm not good expressing myself and that never upsets me until moments like this when I really need words to work.<br/><br/>I'm in love with the Lumatere Chronicles series. Even when it broke my heart at one point, I will probably read it again in the future because this was perfection, from be</span>
  <span id="freeText17128674567628250478" style="display:none">Reading a Marchetta, always:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/657526.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>_______________<br>Re-read 2020 under quarantine. Just as perfect as the first time.<br> <br><b>...leaning on the side of wonder.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390329968ra/8192424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390329968ra/8192425.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm genuinely moved by this series, I really am. I'm not good with words, I'm not good expressing myself and that never upsets me until moments like this when I really need words to work.<br><br>I'm in love with the Lumatere Chronicles series. Even when it broke my heart at one point, I will probably read it again in the future because this was perfection, from beginning to end.<br><br><b> Every character, every love story and every tragedy was so brilliantly portrayed they stopped being ficionals characters a while ago</b>. I've read amazing books in the past but I suspect it's only with Marchetta's stories that I fall completely and undoubtedly in love with them. She could make thousands of spin-offs (C. Clare Style) and I wouldn't mind a bit. I know I'd never get enough of Froi and Quintana, Isaboe and Finn, Luc-ien and Phaedra, Arjuro, Gargarin and Lirah.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390330299i/8192505._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Even if the story gets predictable sometimes (and I say sometimes because there was some serious shit I didn't see coming) Marchetta writes in a way that you just want to live it through, you're in for the journey.<br><br>In my bookish life, I've cried only once and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a> is to blame, until now. You know, just a few tears. <i>Sob of laughter</i>, as Marchetta likes to describe it. Because there were moments like this when I broke:<br><br><b>
  <i>'A pledge, with you blood mixed with ours,' Finnikin said.<br>Froi nodded, unable to speak.<br>'Brothers always. Balthazar is with us, too. We make this work,' Finnikin said fiercely. 'We bring peace to these kingdoms. We deserve it. Our women do. All of us have lost too much, Froi. We've lost the joy of being children. Let's not take that from Jasmina and Tariq and those who come after them.'</i>
</b><br><br>Yeah, that did it. <br>Finn's intensity and fierceness did it. <br><br>The love of this brothers, the memory of what was lost, the greedy hope for a better future and Jasmina and Tariq as a reminder of what can't be destroyed... and I thought of Evanjalin and the useless, wild princess. I though of every sacrifice, every scar, the misery and the courage. <br><br><b>
  <i>Oh, you've outdone me twice, you queen of forgiveness. The ring's a promise of peace and I'm greedy with hope. It's a song that we sing in a tongue that we share. And though you say it's a gift from a king to a king, I say it's a sign from a queen to a queen.</i>
</b><br><br>This is amazing not just because is about our beloved Isaboe but look how mature and lovely Quintana sounds, once wild and unpredictable. <br><br>I have so much I'd like to say about this book yet words seems to fail me, so I'll just say that it's one of the best YA Fantasy I've ever read and not just because the amazing world building, perfect character development or exquisite writing but because inexplicably this books feel like home to me. They belong to me as much as I belong to them.<br><br><b>
  <i>'When do you get to be ours for always?' he asked, his voice low.<br>'Do I have to be here to belong to you?' Froi asked. 'Can't I belong to you wherever I am?'</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17128674567628250478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1535708576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535708576" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1535708576?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=speshul-snowflake">speshul-snowflake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=hmm-that-was-interesting">hmm-that-was-interesting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=aussie-kool-aid">aussie-kool-aid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-loved">books-i-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=wish-that-was-me">wish-that-was-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1535708576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3532527316441874815">The whole time I was reading this book, I was thinking "<i>This</i>. This is what those Syrian refugees are experiencing. The despair, the frustration, the terror, the unexpected acts of kindness, the persistent hope for a better future..." For a book that is not, presumably, written as an allegory, it is eerie how representative this book (and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a>) are of the state of affairs today.<br/><br/>I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_' title='Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a>. It was a mostly straightforward epic fantasy-type book, written beautifully </span>
  <span id="freeText3532527316441874815" style="display:none">The whole time I was reading this book, I was thinking "<i>This</i>. This is what those Syrian refugees are experiencing. The despair, the frustration, the terror, the unexpected acts of kindness, the persistent hope for a better future..." For a book that is not, presumably, written as an allegory, it is eerie how representative this book (and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>) are of the state of affairs today.<br /><br />I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>. It was a mostly straightforward epic fantasy-type book, written beautifully (as is usual for Marchetta), and moving and engaging from the first word to the very last. But the other two books in this series are an entirely different beast. They are scary, thought-provoking, heartbreaking and yet full of the poignancy and humor that afflict everyday life. <br /><br />Froi, oh Froi... what a journey for a "little feef" from the streets of Sarnak. I fell a little in love with Froi way back in Finnkin, when he had a couple of chapters from his POV. And he just grew and grew and grew from thereon, until he now firmly holds a piece of my heart (Marcus Darling, move over!)<br /><br />Isaboe was possibly the most annoying thing in these books. I have noticed that a consistent fantasy trope in these epics fantasy is to make sure that the ruler of a kingdom, especially when they are a protagonist, or otherwise a sympathetic character, is often forced to make "hard decisions" and these decisions generally tend to be of the type that calls for the abandonment/death of another sympathetic character/cause for "the greater good". Whatever, man. Isaboe's consistent hostility to the Charyn refugees often felt like those Americans and Europeans who refuse to accept the refugees because "all Muslims are bad" (yes, yes, that's a redactive statement, but mostly true), or "they will impose Sharia law in our country". Yes, you have suffered at the hands of the bad apples, but when you cannot see beyond the imposed identity of a peoples to the common suffering at the hands of a common enemy, you stop being a sympathetic character. I don't think Isaboe was all that great a queen, frankly, despite what all those characters kept reiterating. (Like in Scandal, where people keep trying SO hard to keep Fitz in office, saying he is a "great President", when really, none of his actions actually prove any such thing). <br /><br />These two books (Froi and Quintana) are a beautifully written tale, and one of the best illustrations of the resilience of the human spirit that I have every seen. Terrible, terrible things perpetrated by terrible, terrible people happen to the protagonists (and a bunch of other people) in these books. But none of those terrible things ever quite manage to overcome the hope and honor and humor of the people living between these pages.<br /><br />As a lifelong fantasy enthusiast, I have to point out that there is minimal worldbuilding, some characters/storylines are mentioned in passing, or just vanish without resolutions (the heir of Yutlind Sud, anyone?) and there are many, many tropes that regular fantasy readers will recognize in an instant. But the thing is, this series is not beautiful in the same way a Sanderson book is beautiful. A Sanderson book is technically perfect (and amazing and riveting and all the other good words), but this series is beautiful in spite of its lack of technical perfection, because of the warmth and <b>realness</b> (not a real word, I know!) permeating every character and every scene. <br /><br />Read it, read it, read it. But beware - it'll make you cry. A lot.<br /><br />(But maybe not as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_" title="Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of the Forest</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3532527316441874815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_422252523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422252523" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422252523?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422252523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5185236380476005865">How do you even begin to do justice on a review for such an amazing end to a truly amazing series? I have yet to read a better series because <b>
  <u>1) the stories had me intrigued; 2) the characters moved me and 3) the books made me think the whole way through and kept me on my toes.</u>
</b><br/><br/>First of all, I think it's a bit of a misnomer that the book was entitled "Quintana of Charyn" because I thought this book was going to be about her. I actually didn't see very much from her perspective, and I felt she</span>
  <span id="freeText5185236380476005865" style="display:none">How do you even begin to do justice on a review for such an amazing end to a truly amazing series? I have yet to read a better series because <b>
  <u>1) the stories had me intrigued; 2) the characters moved me and 3) the books made me think the whole way through and kept me on my toes.</u>
</b><br /><br />First of all, I think it's a bit of a misnomer that the book was entitled "Quintana of Charyn" because I thought this book was going to be about her. I actually didn't see very much from her perspective, and I felt she showed far more character development in book 2. This book was about SO much more. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />•Of course, Quintana's adventures as she carries the future of not only Charyn but of all the lands with impending war;<br />•Froi in his journey to figure out where he truly belongs;<br />•Finnikin and his pride of not being good enough through jealousies when it comes to Isaboe and his role as a consort or a king;<br />•Isaboe as she tries to be a good mother, wife and friend having lost the innocence of childhood - in which she compares with Quintana - and decisions she has to make concerning what is best for her kingdom as she tries to keep her people out of war while still recovering from losing her family;<br />•Lucian as he struggles to follow his father's footsteps as a leader and the battle he faces between his pride and his love for Phaedra;<br />•Phaedra and her coming to terms with being considered useless all her life to finding the strength to protect her queen and reconcile her marriage;<br />•Tesadora and Perri in rekindling their bond and seeing how they fit in their roles (and their child) in this book;<br />•Gargarin and Arjuro and the suffering they have endured and how they come to terms with the mistakes they have made and rise above it all to be two very powerful men;<br />•And so, so many other characters from the Charynite girls in the cave and the lastborns to each soldier, spy, traitor and political contributor. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Each character - no matter how big or small - played their role in each intricate detail of this elaborate web Marchetta has woven.</u>
</b> For me, the stars of this book were Lucian and Phaedra (much like Trevanion and Beatriss in book 2) because the two of them showed far more character development than all of the other characters combined. I was very moved by their love for each other, as well as each one's own struggles (that I mentioned in the first spoiler).<br /><br />But going back to the point, Marchetta created such masterpieces because <b>
  <u>this book, and all the others for that matter, had it all</u>
</b> - past tragedies and how they have brought such suffering to the land, action and adventure as the characters made their journeys through the land, strong character development from all of those involved, and such a clean yet masterful way everything tied together in the end.<br /><br />The kicker was that <b>
  <u>the gears in my head were constantly turning</u>
</b> as I thought of different theories to explain the curse; trying to figure out who was who and who belonged to which parents and how the story of the day of weeping affected each individual character; or guessing what was going to happen next only to have Marchetta throw in another twist. And mind you the twists were never things that made you say, "What the hell?!?" Nope, they were things that Marchetta dropped hints along the way - some you did picked up on and guessed right but some that totally caught you by surprise.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>There were two things that I was disappointed with...</u>
</b> First was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bestiano's death. It was too quick, and almost anticlimatic, and Froi didn't even get the glory. I had expected to have some more satisfaction from that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The other was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I had expected Celie to have a bigger role in the book. With Ferragost, I just thought we would have seen more of her and possibly Valentin Banyon. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But neither disappointments were enough for me to knock down the rating.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>I'm sadden to see the end of such a wonderful series, but I just loved how Marchetta tied it all together</u>
</b> - tidying all of the different side stories; Finnkin coming to terms with his jealousies; Quintana saying hello to everyone like she did when Froi first met her and she greeted everyone at the table despite them not responding back to her; and everyone looking on the side of wonder. <b>
  <u>What a way to come full circle.</u>
</b> Marchetta has truly outdone herself, and I wonder - though totally hoping - if she will ever be able to top this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5185236380476005865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1042618183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1042618183" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1042618183?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=5-star-read">5-star-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=lessons-learned">lessons-learned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=kids-in-the-picture">kids-in-the-picture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=rape">rape</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=romantic-elements">romantic-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=sigh-worthy">sigh-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=with-a-twist">with-a-twist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=favorites-of-all-time">favorites-of-all-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1042618183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13181108656754767475">I couldn't possibly do this series justice with a review. It's honestly unlike anything else I've read...just the style of writing that Melina Marchetta has...it's unique to her. Her characters are flawed...some to the point that you never really <i>like</i> them, but you can certainly <i>relate</i> to them. Quintana is a great example. I don't think I really like her all that much. But I understand her, and she makes Froi happy. There's so much more to that but what a fantastic character. <br/><br/>This is the biggest</span>
  <span id="freeText13181108656754767475" style="display:none">I couldn't possibly do this series justice with a review. It's honestly unlike anything else I've read...just the style of writing that Melina Marchetta has...it's unique to her. Her characters are flawed...some to the point that you never really <i>like</i> them, but you can certainly <i>relate</i> to them. Quintana is a great example. I don't think I really like her all that much. But I understand her, and she makes Froi happy. There's so much more to that but what a fantastic character. <br /><br />This is the biggest selling point of the story for me. While the plot is great and the fantasy is subtle but pervasive, it's how character driven the story is that makes this trilogy stand out. Not one character is even similar to anyone else I've ever read about. You'd think in only three books, I'd not have enough time to become so intensely devoted to everyone, but I did. Finnikin, Isobel, Froi, Trevanion, Lucian, Phaedra, Gargarin, Arjuro...the list goes on and on and on.<br /><br />Are there some things that I wish she'd have added to the story to finish out the "happy ever after" aspect for everyone? Sure. However, the story ending as it did left me feeling like it keeps living on...its the kind of book that I will think of often, and seriously, <b>literally</b> wonder in my head how Froi and Quintana are doing, and are Phaedra and Lucian content now? Is the valley in turmoil now, with all that is going on? What about Rafuel? Did Arjuro sing the souls all home? All the tiny loose ends will play on in my head until I swear the story is never ending. How powerful is that? I read and forget hundreds of books a year. But this series, I'll never forget. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13181108656754767475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154229797?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/912332-wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/912332-wendy?shelf=because-i-can-t-not-read-the-sequal">because-i-can-t-not-read-the-sequal</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/912332-wendy?shelf=read-book-because-i-like-the-author">read-book-because-i-like-the-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/912332-wendy?shelf=reading-for-my-job">reading-for-my-job</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154229797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14695383066107894942">I'm just ... speechless at this point. <br/><br/>I need to ruminate. <br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1349208645p8/590512.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br/>If I could sum up this series with one word, and MM uses it copiously throughout the entire series is <i>
  <b>fierce</b>
</i>. It's a fierce story, full of fierce characters and stories with even fiercer emotions. <br/><br/>It has the ability to tear you to shreds, believe me. <br/><br/>So, last night I finished reading this and I want to say that it just really hasn't hit me yet. The full impact that a story I've invested a good threes years of my lif</span>
  <span id="freeText14695383066107894942" style="display:none">I'm just ... speechless at this point. <br><br>I need to ruminate. <br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1349208645p8/590512.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>If I could sum up this series with one word, and MM uses it copiously throughout the entire series is <i>
  <b>fierce</b>
</i>. It's a fierce story, full of fierce characters and stories with even fiercer emotions. <br><br>It has the ability to tear you to shreds, believe me. <br><br>So, last night I finished reading this and I want to say that it just really hasn't hit me yet. The full impact that a story I've invested a good threes years of my life in. <br><br>I was so so so looking forward to reading this that I think it's almost unfair to have to rate it. Do I give it 5 stars because I just KNEW this would be awesome and epic? Do I give it less because it didn't go in a direction I wanted or was too heartbroken? <br><br>I know that I'm going to re-read this very soon, as there is just a lot going on. In fact, even though I read Froi just a few weeks ago, I think I need to re-read that again too!<br><br>Spoilers below...ye be warned. Also, the more I think of things, I will be adding to this review.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>Lucien, Phaedra...I love you both so much. Without really traveling anywhere (well, a little bit), you have been on the proverbial hero's journey. This plot line was done almost perfectly. I say almost because I want more like a petulant child. More!<br><br>Perri and Tessadora, you two deserve a vacation to a warm sunny beach. Spend some time together without the weight of the world on your shoulders. <br><br>I can't say I was surprised with the baby with Isaboe and Finnikin. It was still a sad shock. But what she did in the cave ... was amazing. <br><br>There was hardly any Beatriss and Trevanion, but since their story was pretty much resolved in the last book, it would have been awkward to introduce more for them to go through. <br><br>We get a glimpse of Celie, and it fits nicely in with what you read in Ferragost. I speak for all fans of this series when I say, "Please, please, please: Melina Marchetta, when you decide to come back to writing novels, we all want more of her story. I think it has the possibility of being a bit more lighthearted and fun, full of intrigue and mystery too."<br><br>Yes, the book has Quintana's name on it, but the first half of the book might be Froi, Continued. Much of it is from Froi's POV, but we all see that it is putting things in motion as the set up for the last act. <br><br>My one complaint: my throat is raw from the continual lump there. I swear, I was on the edge of tears the whole time. Every conversation was just infused with passion and regret, pride and pain. <br><br>I applaud Melina for giving us, her loyal fans, such a wonderful and heartfelt series. If there are major plot holes, I've missed them. If there are cliched characters, or story tropes, I can't find them. I think this was a unique and creative adventure into a Medieval-type society that, I hope, will find it's way into the hands of more and more fans of this historical fantasy genre. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14695383066107894942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_364879582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364879582" />
    <a title="Joie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6224284-joie"><img alt="Joie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453104735p2/6224284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364879582?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joie" href="/user/show/6224284-joie">Joie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=amazeballs">amazeballs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364879582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9187076044450769749"><b>Me before reading a Marchetta book:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383425ra/741639.gif' width='350' height='120' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Me after reading a Marchetta book:</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383425ra/741640.gif' width='300' height='190' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383163ra/741286.gif' width='340' height='210' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Melina Marchetta (authoress divine) is one of those rare authors whose writing is constantly improving, constantly pushing the limits of how much I think I can love a book. When I read FINNIKIN, I felt like I had found The Best Book Ever (aside from Jellicoe Road, of course). But then she wrote FROI and now QUINTANA and I just have no words. At least, none that I haven't said before.<br/><br/>QUINTANA OF CHARYN is, undoubtedly, a conclus</span>
  <span id="freeText9187076044450769749" style="display:none"><b>Me before reading a Marchetta book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383425ra/741639.gif" width="350" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Me after reading a Marchetta book:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383425ra/741640.gif" width="300" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383163ra/741286.gif" width="340" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Melina Marchetta (authoress divine) is one of those rare authors whose writing is constantly improving, constantly pushing the limits of how much I think I can love a book. When I read FINNIKIN, I felt like I had found The Best Book Ever (aside from Jellicoe Road, of course). But then she wrote FROI and now QUINTANA and I just have no words. At least, none that I haven't said before.<br><br>QUINTANA OF CHARYN is, undoubtedly, a conclusion. All the loose ends are tied up and the reader is left in a satisfied place. Actually, it's a rather heart-wrenching place because it's <b>The End</b>, but nevertheless it was a good stopping place. The characters' struggles have been resolved. You know that they're going to be okay, yet there's still an open-endedness that comes with knowing their lives will go on and they will continue to learn and grow.<br><br>With most fantasy books, the authors focus on explaining the world-building. What was great about this series was that yes, Marchetta explained the ways of the Lumaterans, Charynites, and co. But she never took the focus away from the characters and their relationships. At the end of this series, you know these characters: their hopes, their fears, their love of country, and their love for each other. You know their hearts- their very essence. And being so close, so darn attached to these characters made me feel ALL of the feelings.<br><br>While reading, I had the sudden and overwhelming urge to just take all these beloved characters and, I don't know, hide them in my pocket or something. Just snatch them from the pages and tuck them somewhere safe so that they could stop hurting. Maybe that's a little silly, but these characters have just gone through so much in just QUINTANA alone, let alone the entire series. There is pain, devastation, loss, grief, and heartbreak. Yet more powerful than all of that is the undercurrent of hope and love that has been there even in the darkest of times. That is Marchetta's true talent—besides the ability to make me want to curl up into a fetal position and sob— she has the uncanny ability to craft these masterful stories of broken people and their broken relationships and somehow make it a story of redemption and love. <br><br>The Lumatere Chronicles has given me more heartache than I thought possible, yet I always crawl back for more. And, to be honest, I would sooner swear off of chocolate than say goodbye to this series and its magnificent characters. I hate goodbyes. I hate the knowledge that once I finish a book, I will never get to know more about a character's life. But knowing that everyone I cared about in this book ended up okay made saying goodbye just a little bit easier<br><br><b>All in all: </b><br>There's really only one thing to do now...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383425ra/741641.gif" width="340" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm just kidding. <s>No. I'm really not.</s><br><br>Good books give you a beautiful happily ever after. Great books pierce your hearts with sadness and linger on your mind long after you've finished. And then there are the rare, phenomenal books that manage to utterly shatter your heart, then somehow heal you at the end and claim an eternal place in your heart. QUINTANA OF CHARYN is one of those books.<br><br><br><i>*Thank you so much, Candlewick Press and the ladies of <a href="http://132minutes.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">132 Minutes</a> for providing me an arc for review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9187076044450769749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=2012-aussie-challenge">2012-aussie-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=australian">australian</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227422170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4988563297980423159">Well, we've come a long way since the little feef that roamed the streets of Sprie in Sarnak. A long, long way. <br/>Final book in the trilogy, Quintana of Charyn does not disappoint; it's full of joy, horrors, tears and laughter as well. Truth be told, thanks to the grumpy Charynites, it's even more humorous than its predecessors.<br/>As usual, Froi stars in every way, at least for me. The parallel stories all pale in comparison to the strength of this character, whose development throughout the trilogy </span>
  <span id="freeText4988563297980423159" style="display:none">Well, we've come a long way since the little feef that roamed the streets of Sprie in Sarnak. A long, long way. <br />Final book in the trilogy, Quintana of Charyn does not disappoint; it's full of joy, horrors, tears and laughter as well. Truth be told, thanks to the grumpy Charynites, it's even more humorous than its predecessors.<br />As usual, Froi stars in every way, at least for me. The parallel stories all pale in comparison to the strength of this character, whose development throughout the trilogy simply baffles me. Froi is unequivocally the sole, real protagonist of this story and all other characters are satellites that accompany him in his treacherous and painful journey to the fulfillment of his destiny. <br />Needless to say, I loved this book; I felt it even more powerfully than <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>. <br />The only complaint I have is the lack of a glossary. I received my copy of Quintana close to a month ago, but when I started reading I was so frustrated by my inability to recall events and people that I had to put it down and start from the beginning, from <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>. I am sure I would not have appreciated it as much if I hadn't reread the whole thing. Too many characters, politics, places, details to remember. This could have been avoided, had there been a recap in the form of a glossary. <br />Nevertheless, a great story that will stay with me for years to come and that I'll be sure to recommend to whoever is willing to listen. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4988563297980423159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5325425648669684284">I am a shell<br/><br/><br/>this book is a horcrux<br/><br/><br/>ARE BOOKS LEGALLY ALLOWED TO DO THIS<br/><br/><br/></span>
