    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_243454517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/243454517" />
    <a title="Natalie Williamson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5460434-natalie-williamson"><img alt="Natalie Williamson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520349644p2/5460434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/243454517?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Williamson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Williamson" href="/user/show/5460434-natalie-williamson">Natalie Williamson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5460434-natalie-williamson?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5460434-natalie-williamson?shelf=1-read-in-2015">1-read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer243454517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13795804990056468032">Update 11/12/15 - Just realized I've read this series twice this year and I REGRET NOTHING.<br/><br/>Update 3/10/15 - Five million stars forever.<br/><br/><br/>I know I said I was going to wait until I'd done a series re-read before I wrote this review, but, well, I lied. Because I just can't stop thinking about this book, and I really haven't been able to since I finished it at 2:30 this morning (It's gonna be a yawn-filled day). It was that good. It was incredible. And I know that I will revisit this review soon, when</span>
  <span id="freeText13795804990056468032" style="display:none">Update 11/12/15 - Just realized I've read this series twice this year and I REGRET NOTHING.<br /><br />Update 3/10/15 - Five million stars forever.<br /><br /><br />I know I said I was going to wait until I'd done a series re-read before I wrote this review, but, well, I lied. Because I just can't stop thinking about this book, and I really haven't been able to since I finished it at 2:30 this morning (It's gonna be a yawn-filled day). It was that good. It was incredible. And I know that I will revisit this review soon, when I finally make it to the end of <i>Quintana</i> again, but for now I just need to get my thoughts on the page. So here goes.<br /><br />Melina Marchetta has a talent for writing these characters that worm their way into your heart and stay there. (Hands up if you love Thomas Mackee!) And with the Lumatere Chronicles, and <i>Quintana</i> in particular, it's like you can't turn the page without finding another one. And I'm not talking the kind of love where you fawn over them all the time and babble about how perfect they are. I'm talking about the kind of love where you want to smack them upside the head when they are being stupid, hug them to you tight when they're sad, and be a part of the joke when they're laughing. Because these characters are so human that it hurts, in the best possible way. And Marchetta makes you want what they want and dream what they dream, and she does this so well for all of them that you find yourself torn because they don't always want the same thing as each other and how can you possibly choose?<br /><br />Here are some examples. I'll start with Lucian. Lucian, how I love you! From his first exchange with Finnikin in <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> I loved him. The snark! The rivalry! The blood pledge! Oh my! And then in <i>Froi</i> I loved him even more, even when I wanted to take him by the shoulders and shake him. And then, if it's even possible, in this book I loved him <i>more</i>. Because of his fleece and Phaedra and how he still struggles with feeling inadequate as a leader for his people. How he shows with his actions that he is anything but.<br /><br />And Phaedra, girl, you go! She took a while to win me over in <i>Froi</i>, but boy, did she. Her strength in the valley, and then in making such a difficult decision to protect the future of her country. And just pretty much everything in this book. I want to be BFFs with Phaedra. For eva and eva.<br /><br />Then there's Gargarin and Lirah and Arjuro and DeLancey. And Trevanion and Beatriss and Vestie and Yata and the cows, Bert and Gert, and Rafuel and Cora and Jorja and Florenza. And Tesadora and Perri and Japhra. And everyone in the valley and in Lumatere and everywhere. All of them. Except for Bestiano. <br /><br />And Finnikin, who chooses to drown in hope rather than float into nothing. And Froi, who learns to stop counting to keep himself from smashing people. Whoever thought that the little thief from Sarnak could do so much? And the things he says and does in this book? Wow. Just, wow. Froi forever has a space in my heart. I love both Finn and Froi, but I think Froi wins. A little. Oh, who am I kidding? I can't choose. And then there's Quintana with her snarl and her coldness and her worries for the little King. I think one of the things I loved best was getting to know her better in this book. Getting to hear her song to Froi. It made me love her more. I know I keep saying this, about everyone, but it's true. I am full of love. That's what Melina Marchetta does, I'm telling you.<br /><br />And then, last but not least, Isaboe. Isaboe has been one of my favorite characters from her first appearance in <i>Finnikin</i>, but I didn't always agree with her actions. She is fierce, and stubborn, and wise, and often right, and sometimes that's hard to accept. She often does the hard thing, and sticks with her convictions even when it makes others uncomfortable. And even though I loved and admired her character, I didn't always like her. But then this books happens, and there are two moments, one huge and gut-wrenching, one small but equally gut-wrenching, that made me forget every time I was ever mad at her and remember all the reasons I loved her. They made me think about the kind of person I want to be. And it was the small one, a scene near the very end, that made me cry. Thank you, Ms. Marchetta, for handing my heart to me on a platter. <br /><br />I won't go into story details, because this doesn't come out in the US until March, and because I don't want to ruin anything. But I will say this: there were moments when I laughed out loud, and moments where I had to put the book down because I was like, OMG what just happened! And, as mentioned above, there were moments when I cried, and let me tell you, I am not a crier. <br /><br />Basically, read it. Read it if you've read <i>Finnkin</i> and <i>Froi</i> or if you haven't (but start at the beginning if you haven't read those two). Then read all of Marchetta's other books and ask yourself how you've gone so long without them. That's what I did when I read <i>Jellicoe</i> for the first time. This one too. They're that good.<br /><br />Okay, rant over. Hopefully it made sense. I'm off to re-read <i>Finnikin</i> again. And maybe take a nap. If I find the time.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13795804990056468032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_293881538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293881538" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293881538?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293881538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16665985863543294532"><i>
  <b>Check out this review and others like it at <a href='www.badassbookreviews.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>BadAssBookReviews</a></b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a>, where the heck do you get your ideas? I can't think of very many authors who are able to cross over into a different genre and successfully write a brilliant and captivating novel? *drums fingers on table* <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3472.Margaret_Atwood' title='Margaret Atwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>Margaret Atwood</a>? <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King' title='Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stephen King</a>? <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling' title='J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.K. Rowling</a>? I guess it depends on how we are determining the distinction between genres. What is clear is that Marchetta’s earlier books are realistic young adult fiction and the</span>
  <span id="freeText16665985863543294532" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Check out this review and others like it at <a href="www.badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">BadAssBookReviews</a></b>
</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a>, where the heck do you get your ideas? I can't think of very many authors who are able to cross over into a different genre and successfully write a brilliant and captivating novel? *drums fingers on table* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3472.Margaret_Atwood" title="Margaret Atwood" rel="nofollow noopener">Margaret Atwood</a>? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a>? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a>? I guess it depends on how we are determining the distinction between genres. What is clear is that Marchetta’s earlier books are realistic young adult fiction and the Lumatere Chronicles are epic fantasy. I do, however, see some striking similarities betweens her earlier books and this fantasy trilogy.<br /><br />The Characters. The Lumatere Chronicles tell the story of people who have been affected by war. Many fantasy books tell the story of nations, kingdoms, magic, families, etc. but Marchetta’s fantasy trilogy is primarily focused on individual characters. The structure of the story, the creation of the world and the political issues are well done but their strength lies, in my opinion, in being a beautifully deep and textured setting for the characters to interact. <br /><br />The Pain. If you have not read a Marchetta novel before – and I have only read one (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>) - -then you might not know that Marchetta has a talent for writing about emotional pain embedded so deep that people are forever altered by their past experiences. She is somehow able to take a starting point, where an individual is seemingly damaged and then weave in the past in a non-preachy way that instead of being confusing or boring is done so skillfully that as a reader I am not sure if I want to be living in the character’s past or the character’s present. <br /><br />The Joy. There is so much mystery and pain in this trilogy that the end is damned satisfying. It isn’t perfect, but it just feels …. Well-earned. My one complaint is that I saw the resolution of all the problems from the beginning of the book and okay, I have two complaints - -the epilogue was just a little to neat and wrapped up for my dark tastes. But ultimately, I still really enjoyed this trilogy, this book and I still cried with joy at the end.<br /><br />The sexual tension is delicious and slow building. The men and women are equally matched; there is give and take and there is truly no submission by one to the other except for perhaps by both together to each other. <br /><br />I highly recommend this series to fans of Marchetta, fans of epic fantasy who also enjoy character driven novels. And if you were not thrilled with the first in this series, I promise you that it is worth it to stick with this series. The second book in the Lumatere Chronicles (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>) is amazing and Quintana perhaps matches Froi. So if you thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> was only a 3 star book, keep going. You will not be sorry. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16665985863543294532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5TjMx4l5LyP7dpEk2+VXvHO/aBlDY5HgWESWLB0sqCv91xZSfwg+t8Usf3xkUoksxPMpoMntXbwNiwz3+B/etg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ekUsru1bW2o7eG4xVJI64QMACmlSUyGEBtXjlPl2pJJiqvY7GypK/gUigGnrJeRxtExL0Njd7dhTGnlPHEXSDw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4276923301870815880">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the </span>
  <span id="freeText4276923301870815880" style="display:none">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the Jellicoe Road was released in 2006 and won the US Printz Medal in 2009 for excellence in YA literature. This was followed up by Finnikin of the Rock in 2008 which won the Aurealis Award for YA fantasy, The Piper's Son in 2010 which was shortlisted for the Qld Premier's Lit Award, NSW Premier's Lit Award, Prime Minister's Literary Awards, CBC awards and longlisted for the Miles Franklin Award. Her follow up to Finnikin, Froi of the Exiles and Quintana of Charyn were released in 2012 and 2013. Her latest novel Tell the Truth, Shame the Devil is an adult crime novel.</span>
